  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a85ccf0f-c156-4795-8dd9-8b362cd83384'
      });
    }

<div id="review_2177703121" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2177703121" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2177703121?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2177703121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5562240532388926026"><b><u>This is not</u> going to include anything to do with the actual Cirque Du Freak</b><br/><br/>You have been warned. I know, I was pretty devastated too...<br/><br/>It's not a bad book. Darren has settled into vampire life somewhat well but upon summons by the Vampire Council, both he and Mr. Crepsley have to trek to <b>Vampire Mountain</b> to plead their case. <br/><br/>Throughout the book, we are given snitches and tidbits of what vampire society is like - <b>
  <u>harsh, cruel and noble.</u>
</b> The author has <b>no qualms</b> about depicting <b>gruesome detail</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5562240532388926026" style="display:none"><b><u>This is not</u> going to include anything to do with the actual Cirque Du Freak</b><br /><br />You have been warned. I know, I was pretty devastated too...<br /><br />It's not a bad book. Darren has settled into vampire life somewhat well but upon summons by the Vampire Council, both he and Mr. Crepsley have to trek to <b>Vampire Mountain</b> to plead their case. <br /><br />Throughout the book, we are given snitches and tidbits of what vampire society is like - <b>
  <u>harsh, cruel and noble.</u>
</b> The author has <b>no qualms</b> about depicting <b>gruesome details. </b><br /><br />Characters die, often painfully and without a 'reason.' I keep expecting (as seen with other middle school books) for the character's death to <b> further plot or provide character development. </b> Here, the characters die because they were in the wrong place at the wrong time. <b>Chillingly real.</b><br /><br />I was a bit annoyed by the ending - we spend all this time building and nothing is played out. <b>ALSO</b> there's no Cirque du Freak. I picked up this series cause I adored all the cirque characters but we don't see any of them. Highly disappointing.<br /><br /><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br />Read by Ralph Lister - and he did a lovely job of it.<br /><br /><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5562240532388926026" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1156090131" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1156090131" />
    <a title="Kyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9740056-kyle"><img alt="Kyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481754383p2/9740056.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1156090131?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kyle" href="/user/show/9740056-kyle">Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780316041812" href="/book/show/7000253-vampire-mountain">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1156090131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4040502247297719941"><div>
  <p>Good read but frustrating ending…</p>
  <p>So great story, the plot is building, it’s really starting to get good and then, TO BE CONTINUED…</p>
  <p>Really? The book is only 212 pages long! I get that the author is writing these for a young audience but we can sit and read a book that’s longer than 200 pages. The Harry Potter series should have proven that. If you’re going to publish a book then make it a complete story for crying out loud. Right now I just feel cheated. If the rest of the series ends up </p></div></span>
  <span id="freeText4040502247297719941" style="display:none"><div>
  <p>Good read but frustrating ending…</p>
  <p>So great story, the plot is building, it’s really starting to get good and then, TO BE CONTINUED…</p>
  <p>Really? The book is only 212 pages long! I get that the author is writing these for a young audience but we can sit and read a book that’s longer than 200 pages. The Harry Potter series should have proven that. If you’re going to publish a book then make it a complete story for crying out loud. Right now I just feel cheated. If the rest of the series ends up being the same, not sure I’m willing to invest my time in it. </p>
  <p>To read my review of the other books in this series, use the links below:</p>
  <blockquote>
      Book One: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1156090036" rel="nofollow noopener">A Living Nightmare</a> <br />	 Book Two: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1156090062" rel="nofollow noopener">The Vampire's Assistant</a> <br />	 Book Three: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1156090092" rel="nofollow noopener">Tunnels of Blood</a> <br />	 Book Five: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1671698784" rel="nofollow noopener">Trials of Death</a> <br />	 Book Six: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1559712336" rel="nofollow noopener">The Vampire Prince</a> <br />	 Book Seven: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1156090221" rel="nofollow noopener">Hunters of the Dusk</a> <br /> 
  </blockquote>

<div id="review_110456760" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110456760" />
    <a title="Paul Eckert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2894762-paul-eckert"><img alt="Paul Eckert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442508071p2/2894762.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110456760?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Eckert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Eckert" href="/user/show/2894762-paul-eckert">Paul Eckert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110456760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6800594233856093351">This marks the fourth book I've read in the Cirque Du Freak series, and I keep expecting to be disappointed, waiting for the magic to run out. Thankfully, the series is still strong and still gripping. <br/><br/>One of the things I like best about the Cirque Du Freak series is that the protagonist, Darren Shan (yes, also the author's name...which I thought was a pretty hilarious thing to do, thought I bet his intention was to make it more 'real' for the young adult audience), never has an easy time. Consi</span>
  <span id="freeText6800594233856093351" style="display:none">This marks the fourth book I've read in the Cirque Du Freak series, and I keep expecting to be disappointed, waiting for the magic to run out. Thankfully, the series is still strong and still gripping. <br /><br />One of the things I like best about the Cirque Du Freak series is that the protagonist, Darren Shan (yes, also the author's name...which I thought was a pretty hilarious thing to do, thought I bet his intention was to make it more 'real' for the young adult audience), never has an easy time. Considering that the series is twelve books long, it's almost a given that he isn't going to die. But he is constantly making tough choices and put in difficult situations that constantly build his character. I'm a sucker for characters that strive to better themselves, or that become stronger characters throughout the story. <br /><br />In this installment, Darren and Mr. Crepsley (his vampire mentor) make the trek to Vampire Mountain (if I have any gripe against the CDF stories, it is that the names can be a bit corny). Vampire Mountain is essentially headquarters for the vampire race. But getting to the mountain is far from easy, and vampires pride themselves on being tough resilient creatures. <br /><br />This book lacks much direct conflict, with the exception of few fight scenes. Additionally, there is a lot of tension built around a predicted war with the vampaneze (another corny name). But the real fun in this book is how much the reader learns about the vampires. Much of the information is revealed in dialogue, which is usually a no-no in fiction, but Shan writes it so smoothly that it's easily forgivable. Moreover, the world of the vampires is quite interesting and combines familiar legend with unique world-building on Shan's part. <br /><br />I'll be diving into book #5 momentarily...</span>
  <a data-text-id="6800594233856093351" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9154985758981730602">2 stars seems a little generous for this, since the book had nothing to offer, so 1,5 it is.   <span id="freeText9154985758981730602" style="display:none">2 stars seems a little generous for this, since the book had nothing to offer, so 1,5 it is. It was basically an infodump about the "broader universe" just to set up the next book, with a little bit of "Darren's life in Cirque du Freak has gone stale so we have to move on" in the beginning. Just when I was expecting some action, the -already short- book ended.<br /><br />Not to mention a terribly sexist remark at one point: "There aren't many vampire women because we can't have children" Obviously, when a woman can't have a child, she has no purpose in life, amiright?? No matter that there are women who physically can't have children in real life. Awesome. But what did I even expect from a series that has had a whooping five (5) women with "supporting" speaking roles so far, in the entire series?</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer59337247" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1752595254614772759">This is the fourth book in the Cirque Du Freak series. In this series Darren Shan assumes the role of a half vampire and travels with Mr Crepsley as he learns more about his new powers of a vampire and he adapts to the standards and needs of a new vampire life. In this book, Darren has to travel to vampire mountain, the journey can take months and they are forced to travel on bare feet. On the way to the mountain with Mr Crepsley, they met Gavner Purl, a Vampire General who was following Mr Crep</span>
  <span id="freeText1752595254614772759" style="display:none">This is the fourth book in the Cirque Du Freak series. In this series Darren Shan assumes the role of a half vampire and travels with Mr Crepsley as he learns more about his new powers of a vampire and he adapts to the standards and needs of a new vampire life. In this book, Darren has to travel to vampire mountain, the journey can take months and they are forced to travel on bare feet. On the way to the mountain with Mr Crepsley, they met Gavner Purl, a Vampire General who was following Mr Crepsley to vampire mountain. On the way they also met a pack of wolves to go to the Council to pick up the leftover food there. When they got there, they met up with the other Vampire Generals such as Mika Ver Leth, Arrow, Vanez, the oldest vampire, Paris, Mr Crepsley's fiance, Arra Sails, and a friend vampire named Kurda Smahlt<br /> I can relate this book to the world because many people are called everyday to arrange a party of some sort. When they arrive, they have chats of old memories, of recent activities and such and they just socialize, in book 4, Vampire Mountain, of the Cirque Du Freak Series, they also travel a long harsh way just to meet about their fellow vampires and then socialize like normal and have duels.<br /> I rate this book a 5 because just like the other books of the Cirque Du Freak Series, it is well paced, and beautifully written, I would recommend this book to anybody just finding a book to read, this series will keep you reading for a while. I also personally find it hard to put down because Darren is a teenager in this book and he needs to go through relationships personally and with others as well. </span>

<div id="review_2055510459" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2055510459" />
    <a title="Joel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14109930-joel"><img alt="Joel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375406751p2/14109930.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2055510459?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joel" href="/user/show/14109930-joel">Joel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14109930-joel?shelf=yearly-reads-2017">yearly-reads-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2055510459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9975401541650421380">Don't know really what happened with this one. It seems that perhaps the publisher might have pressured Mr. Shan to split a book in two, because this one is only half a book. Most of the book was used to do some infodumping and then end a cliffhanger. Still like the characters and where the story is going, but it was quite disappointing especially compared to how good the last one was which so far it has been the high point of the series. But hey, these books are short and fun, and the violence </span>
  <span id="freeText9975401541650421380" style="display:none">Don't know really what happened with this one. It seems that perhaps the publisher might have pressured Mr. Shan to split a book in two, because this one is only half a book. Most of the book was used to do some infodumping and then end a cliffhanger. Still like the characters and where the story is going, but it was quite disappointing especially compared to how good the last one was which so far it has been the high point of the series. But hey, these books are short and fun, and the violence and gore is delightfully shocking and disturbing for a middle-grade book. I recommend this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9975401541650421380" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_440224693" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/440224693" />
    <a title="Julianna Martinez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13893303-julianna-martinez"><img alt="Julianna Martinez" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julianna Martinez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julianna Martinez" href="/user/show/13893303-julianna-martinez">Julianna Martinez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer440224693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7554881167450627052">Book Report Guidelines – Good Reads<br/>Name of book: Vampire Mountain <br/>Author: Darren Shan<br/>Pages: 208<br/>Genre: Fiction<br/>Reading Level of book: <br/><br/>Exposition (4-6 sentences)<br/>In Vampire Mountain, Darren is a half-vampire. He is Mr. Crepsley’s assistant. Mr. Crepsley is the Vampire that turned Darren into a half-vampire. Mr.Crepsley tould Darren that they will be leaving the Cirque Du Freak because Mr. Crepsley had to present Darren to the Vampire Council. The Council only meets once every twelve years. They have</span>
  <span id="freeText7554881167450627052" style="display:none">Book Report Guidelines – Good Reads<br />Name of book: Vampire Mountain <br />Author: Darren Shan<br />Pages: 208<br />Genre: Fiction<br />Reading Level of book: <br /><br />Exposition (4-6 sentences)<br />In Vampire Mountain, Darren is a half-vampire. He is Mr. Crepsley’s assistant. Mr. Crepsley is the Vampire that turned Darren into a half-vampire. Mr.Crepsley tould Darren that they will be leaving the Cirque Du Freak because Mr. Crepsley had to present Darren to the Vampire Council. The Council only meets once every twelve years. They have to go on a journey through the mountains without using any of their Vampire abilities.<br /><br />Conflict: (4-6 sentences)<br />On their journey, Darren and Mr. Crepsley found Vampire coffins, and they encountered a Vampaneze Bear. When Darren arrived at Vampire Mountain, he took a tour of the halls. Darren competed in a game. He had to compete against Arra, of the girl vampires. He competed with her because he wanted to earn her respect, and the Princes heard about that and they were surprised. Darren and Arra fenced, and when Darren beat Arra, he earned her respect.<br /><br />Climax: (4-6 sentences)<br />When Mr. Crepsley presents Darren to the Vampire Princes, they don’t like that Mr. Crepsley blooded a child. They disapprove because it was against the rules to blood a child. Mr. Crepsley told them not to punish Darren, but to punish him because it was his fault. Since Mr. Crepsley had a history with the Princes, they respected him, and gave him a chance to prove the boy worthy. The Vampire Princes said that Darren has to show that he is worthy of being in the Vampire Ranks.<br /><br />Resolution: (4-6 sentences)<br />In order for Darren to show he is worthy, he has to complete the Trails of Death. The Trails of Death is a test. Darren learns that if he passes, he will be accepted into the Vampire Ranks. However, if he fails, or quits, he will be killed. Darren’s adventure continues onto the next book.<br /><br /><br />Choose a theme in your book and compare to any piece of literature we have read in class. What is similar? What is different? What have you learned about the human experience? (7-10 sentences)<br /><br />A theme of Vampire Mountain would be friendship. It is similar to The Perks of Being a Wallflower. In The Perks of Being a Wallflower, Charlie makes two friends who he thought were funny, and he connected to. In Vampire Mountain, Darren found two friends as well. They were Vampires who were much older than him, and he used their advice to help him understand the ways of a Vampire. Similarly, Charlie received advice from his older friends about his life and being weird. Additionally, these two books are similar in that Charlie is a teenager going through hard times, and Darren is a young kid trying to understand the world. In Perks of Being a Wallflower, Charlie is lonely and sensitive, but in Vampire Mountain, Darren is tough, and confident. In the end, Charlie makes friends and is no longer alone, but Darren has to take a bigger risk and be alone. Both books teach that no matter where you come from, you’ll always be similar to someone.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7554881167450627052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer59038240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1576005915985697416"> Vampire Mountain<br/>	By: Darren Shan<br/><br/>ISBN: 0316905747<br/>208 Pages<br/>Publisher: Little Brown Young Readers<br/>2004<br/><br/>	Vampire Mountain Is the 4th book of the cirque du freak series. It is as great of a book as the others. But now Darren and Mr. Crepsly are traveling to take several trails for Darren Will Darren pass them and continue his life? Or does it all ends at the trails? Darren Shan continues his great work of description. His new characters are just unbelievably amazing. Darren just continues on with this</span>
  <span id="freeText1576005915985697416" style="display:none"> Vampire Mountain<br />	By: Darren Shan<br /><br />ISBN: 0316905747<br />208 Pages<br />Publisher: Little Brown Young Readers<br />2004<br /><br />	Vampire Mountain Is the 4th book of the cirque du freak series. It is as great of a book as the others. But now Darren and Mr. Crepsly are traveling to take several trails for Darren Will Darren pass them and continue his life? Or does it all ends at the trails? Darren Shan continues his great work of description. His new characters are just unbelievably amazing. Darren just continues on with this great plot and he makes it even greater than before each time.<br />	Darren Shan just continues to describe everything better and better. Each book is another movie playing in your head. When Darren runs into the wolves on his way to Vampire Mountain, and they start to act like dogs. You can just see the wolves, ravage animals at first, then mans best friend. And when he describes them walking to Vampire Mountain, you imagine your self walking towards Vampire Mountain.<br />	Darren’s new characters just made the book even more all the best. They just make this book more and more fantastic. These new vampires make it seem as if it’s the beginning all over. You just want to learn more and more about these characters and continue reading. He gives the characters such great characteristics. You would imagine they are real people he just turned into book characters.<br />	Darren’s plot just gets even better. Each book he makes, everything gets so much better. He continues to write his books better each time. The plot becomes more captive. You would not want to put the book down. All you would want is to find out how things would end out. He makes a ravaging savage wolf turn into a vampire’s best friend. Vampaneze’s trying to kill Darren and his crew, trying to prevent them from reaching Vampire Mountain.<br />	Darren Shan never stops writing his awesome stories. He makes them so realistic and so imaginable. His plots in each book gets better and better. His descriptions are just amazing. The characters are just great. You will die of reading hunger from reading this book. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1576005915985697416" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Nikki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29166340-nikki"><img alt="Nikki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438297005p2/29166340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1260050833?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nikki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nikki" href="/user/show/29166340-nikki">Nikki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1260050833&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1260050833" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1849206522298219945">This was another good book in the cirque du freak series that didn't let it down not one bit, it was about Darren and Mr Crepsley's Journey to Vampire mountain, where they would seek counsel with the vampire princes about Darren being blooded by Mr Crepsley. This wasn't an easy journey they weren't allowed to flit, they had to do it all almost like a human, in the cold wet dark and dangerous woods, land, caves. They met a few characters along the way bears and vampinese and wolves who they befri</span>
  <span id="freeText1849206522298219945" style="display:none">This was another good book in the cirque du freak series that didn't let it down not one bit, it was about Darren and Mr Crepsley's Journey to Vampire mountain, where they would seek counsel with the vampire princes about Darren being blooded by Mr Crepsley. This wasn't an easy journey they weren't allowed to flit, they had to do it all almost like a human, in the cold wet dark and dangerous woods, land, caves. They met a few characters along the way bears and vampinese and wolves who they befriended, as you can guess they definitely did make it to the mountain. Darren had to face an insane bear in the woods on the way to the mountain and luckily he wasn't killed. When he finally got to the mountain he was intrigued as to the ways of the ancient vampires lived, worked and hunted and learnt a little more knowledge about the legends and myths surrounding the vampires. He even managed to have a sports fight in the hall of sports. <br /><br />Evra and Darren no longer seem close not as they have done in previous books, this was a shame because they bounced off each other so easily, they were almost like brothers not friends but well that seemed to have dissapeared in this book.<br /><br />Darren and Mr Crepsley seem to be getting on a lot better almost forming a strong friendship, Darren even got Mr Cresley to laugh, Mr Crepsley seems to finally treating Darren as less than a child. <br /><br />This book was really descriptive which wasn't a drag but a good thing. Some of the scenes were so well described it felt as if you were there a part of it not a reader of a book. The histories of vampires were interesting to read and cause you to wonder. This wasn't as action packed as others in the series which left me a little flat but it didn't dissapoint. <br /><br />I'll be reading the next one in the series.</span>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Parker O&#39;connor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Parker O&#39;connor" href="/user/show/34636249-parker-o-connor">Parker O&#39;connor</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1287038813" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3984142968482690159">I think Cirque Du Freak Vampire Mountain was a great book. The book was full of great moments. The Vampaneze make a comeback and it is the main issue in the book. Mr. Crepsley and Darren decide to go to Vampire Mountain for the meeting of the counsel because it only happens every 8 years. It is a terribly hard journey and Mr. Tiny forces them to take two little people along with them. On their way they stop and find a dead vampire. They think he was ambushed by a animal and move on. They then sm</span>
  <span id="freeText3984142968482690159" style="display:none">I think Cirque Du Freak Vampire Mountain was a great book. The book was full of great moments. The Vampaneze make a comeback and it is the main issue in the book. Mr. Crepsley and Darren decide to go to Vampire Mountain for the meeting of the counsel because it only happens every 8 years. It is a terribly hard journey and Mr. Tiny forces them to take two little people along with them. On their way they stop and find a dead vampire. They think he was ambushed by a animal and move on. They then smell vamaneze blood, and find out it was no animal that killed the vampire. They then try to move as fast as possible to alert the vampire princes that the vampaneze could be preparing for war. Along the way they meet a pack of wolves that Darren takes a liking to. They hunt with the wolves every night and the wolves keep watch for danger during the day. Once they arrive Darren presented to the princes. To prove he deserves to be a vampire he has to participate in the Trials of Death, leading into the next book. <br /><br />I gave this book 4 out of 5 stars. The book has a lot of action, but some parts are dragged on for to long. There are some new characters in the book that are very enjoyable to read about. I would of liked more action in the beginning of the book. The first half of the book was just about them climbing the mountain and got boring at times. Overall it was a good book<br /><br />I would recommend this book to middle school and high school boys. The main character is a boy so a male audience could relate to his thoughts more than females could. Boys also tend to like action and fantasy more that girls do.<br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9985866726300485400">I have to say, I didn't enjoy this book as much as i hoped to. I thought it was kind of boring. Like, at some points it could be really interesting but other parts just kind of fell flat. I also think that the first half was a lot better than the second.<br/>In this book a lot of the adults really bugged me. I feel like they thought that just because Darren Was a kid, that meant he wasn't strong or smart. Like, he can do a lot more than what these people give him credit for. I mean, he did make it al</span>
  <span id="freeText9985866726300485400" style="display:none">I have to say, I didn't enjoy this book as much as i hoped to. I thought it was kind of boring. Like, at some points it could be really interesting but other parts just kind of fell flat. I also think that the first half was a lot better than the second.<br />In this book a lot of the adults really bugged me. I feel like they thought that just because Darren Was a kid, that meant he wasn't strong or smart. Like, he can do a lot more than what these people give him credit for. I mean, he did make it all the way to Vampire Mountain without getting seriously injured.<br />In the real world i think grown-ups do that a lot. I think sometimes they do that because they don't want to admit that they are wrong! They think that they are better or don't think that a kid can prove them wrong. <br />It's like the whole this with Arra. When Darren almost beat her on the bars, she got upset. It was like she didn't realize that it was just for fun and that Darren wasn't purposly trying to make her upset. But. at least she kind of opened up and started being at least civil towards Darren.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pOSWMoe28SniIZZWGSf0Rh/3NVu3JpfWzBUuI1DfWp4eTcVAX6LGdBVSnTVqFJQR+GAJJcgpE10qjCmTp7xAAA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JEeGmw+b8WIHEaxyX0Fak7KlIs6ud6/v+iJYA69qEy2e7tXp14/GP/BipxEscjrEVTIesNF4K2Qcu1+zWAkJsw==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText7882149716232170857" style="display:none">Librarian's note: Also writes books for adults under the name <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7790731.Darren_Dash" rel="nofollow noopener">Darren Dash</a>. And in the past he has released books for adults under the names <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1304819.D_B_Shan" rel="nofollow noopener">D.B. Shan</a> and Darren O'Shaughnessy.<br /><br />Darren Shan (born July 2, 1972 in London, England) is the pen name of the Irish author Darren O'Shaughnessy, as well as the name of the protagonist of his book series The Saga of Darren Shan, also known as The Cirque Du Freak Series in the United States. He is the author of the series The Demonata, The Saga of Larten Crepsley, and Zom-B. He has also released the stand-alone novel, The Thin Executioner, and the stand-alone short novels, Koyasan, and Hagurosan. Plus, for adults, he released The City Trilogy (originally under the name of D.B. Shan), and Lady of the Shades.. </span>
